Chinese<br />1.6% other</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">Demonym(s)</a></th><td>Cantabrigian</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">Time zone</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B0" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+0">UTC+0</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">Greenwich Mean Time</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><span style="white-space:nowrap">&#160;•&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</span></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B1" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+1">UTC+1</a> (<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Postcode</th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code"><a href="/wiki/CB_postcode_area" title="CB postcode area">CB1&#160;– CB5</a></div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th><td>01223</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ONS_coding_system" title="ONS coding system">ONS code</a></th><td>12UB (ONS)<br />E07000008 (GSS)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/British_national_grid_reference_system" class="mw-redirect" title="British national grid reference system">OS grid reference</a></th><td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion" style="white-space: nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/en/52.208351125473;0.12065137322994_region:GB_scale:25000?pagename=Cambridge">TL450588</a></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cambridge.gov.uk/">www.cambridge.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Cambridge</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KAYM</span>-brij</i></a>) is a <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">university city</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire" title="Cambridgeshire">Cambridgeshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/River_Cam" title="River Cam">River Cam</a> approximately 50 miles (80&#160;km) north of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">United Kingdom Census 2011</a>, its population was 123,867 including 24,506 students.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge became an important trading centre during the Roman and Viking ages, and there is archaeological evidence of settlement in the area as early as the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Town_charter#Municipal_charters" class="mw-redirect" title="Town charter">town charters</a> were granted in the 12th century, although modern city status was not officially conferred until 1951.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> was founded in 1209.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  The buildings of the university include <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_Chapel,_Cambridge" title="King&#39;s College Chapel, Cambridge">King's College Chapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cavendish_Laboratory" title="Cavendish Laboratory">Cavendish Laboratory</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Library" title="Cambridge University Library">Cambridge University Library</a>, one of the largest legal deposit libraries in the world. The city's skyline is dominated by several college buildings, along with the spire of the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_and_the_English_Martyrs_Church" title="Our Lady and the English Martyrs Church">Our Lady and the English Martyrs Church</a>, and the chimney of <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's Hospital</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a>, which evolved from the Cambridge School of Art and the Cambridgeshire College of Arts and Technology, also has its main campus in the city.
</p><p>Cambridge is at the heart of the high-technology <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Fen" title="Silicon Fen">Silicon Fen</a> with industries such as <a href="/wiki/Software_industry" title="Software industry">software</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bioscience" class="mw-redirect" title="Bioscience">bioscience</a> and many start-up companies born out of the university. Over 40 per cent of the workforce have a higher education qualification, more than twice the national average. The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Biomedical_Campus" title="Cambridge Biomedical Campus">Cambridge Biomedical Campus</a>, one of the largest biomedical research clusters in the world, is soon to house premises of <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>, a hotel, and the relocated <a href="/wiki/Papworth_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Papworth Hospital">Papworth Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first game of <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> took place at <a href="/wiki/Parker%27s_Piece" title="Parker&#39;s Piece">Parker's Piece</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fair" title="Strawberry Fair">Strawberry Fair</a> music and arts festival and Midsummer Fair are held on <a href="/wiki/Midsummer_Common" title="Midsummer Common">Midsummer Common</a>, and the annual <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Beer_Festival" title="Cambridge Beer Festival">Cambridge Beer Festival</a> takes place on <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Green" title="Jesus Green">Jesus Green</a>. The city is adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/M11_motorway" title="M11 motorway">M11</a> and <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14</a> roads. <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge station</a> is less than an hour from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross railway station</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Cambridge" title="Timeline of Cambridge">Timeline of Cambridge</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">Prehistoric Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Iron_Age" title="British Iron Age">British Iron Age</a></div>
<p>Settlements have existed around the Cambridge area since <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">prehistoric times</a>. The earliest clear evidence of occupation is the remains of a <span class="nowrap">3,500-</span>year-old farmstead discovered at the site of <a href="/wiki/Fitzwilliam_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitzwilliam College">Fitzwilliam College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Archaeological evidence of occupation through the <a href="/wiki/British_Iron_Age" title="British Iron Age">Iron Age</a> is a settlement on <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Cambridge" title="Castle Hill, Cambridge">Castle Hill</a> from the 1st century BC, perhaps relating to wider cultural changes occurring in southeastern Britain linked to the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Belgae" title="Belgae">Belgae</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman">Roman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Roman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duroliponte" title="Duroliponte">Duroliponte</a></div>
<p>The principal <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman</a> site is a small fort (<i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Castrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Castrum">castrum</a></i></i>) <b><a href="/wiki/Duroliponte" title="Duroliponte">Duroliponte</a></b> on <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Cambridge" title="Castle Hill, Cambridge">Castle Hill</a>, just northwest of the city centre around the location of the earlier <a href="/wiki/Britons_(Celtic_people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (Celtic people)">British</a> village. The fort was bounded on two sides by the lines formed by the present <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Pleasant, Cambridge">Mount Pleasant</a>, continuing across <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_Road" title="Huntingdon Road">Huntingdon Road</a> into Clare Street. The eastern side followed Magrath Avenue, with the southern side running near to <a href="/wiki/Chesterton_Lane,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesterton Lane, Cambridge">Chesterton Lane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kettle%27s_Yard" title="Kettle&#39;s Yard">Kettle's Yard</a> before turning northwest at Honey Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It was constructed around AD&#160;70 and converted to civilian use around 50 years later. Evidence of more widespread Roman settlement has been discovered including numerous farmsteads<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and a village in the Cambridge district of <a href="/wiki/Newnham,_Cambridgeshire" title="Newnham, Cambridgeshire">Newnham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Medieval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Roman_withdrawal_from_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman withdrawal from Britain">Roman withdrawal from Britain</a> around 410, the location may have been abandoned by the <a href="/wiki/Romano-Britons" class="mw-redirect" title="Romano-Britons">Britons</a>, although the site is usually identified as <span class="nowrap"><b>Cair Grauth</b></span><sup id="cite_ref-mommy_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mommy-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> listed among the 28 <a href="/wiki/Civitas" title="Civitas">cities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Roman_Britain" title="Sub-Roman Britain">Britain</a> by the <i><a href="/wiki/Historia_Brittonum" title="Historia Brittonum">History of the Britons</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nashford_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nashford-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Evidence exists that the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_invasion_of_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon invasion of Britain">invading Anglo-Saxons</a> had begun occupying the area by the end of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Their settlement – also on and around Castle Hill – became known as <b>Grantebrycge</b><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> ("<a href="/wiki/River_Cam" title="River Cam">Granta</a>-bridge"). (By <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a>, the settlement's name had changed to "Cambridge", and the <a href="/wiki/River_Cam" title="River Cam">lower stretches</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Granta_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Granta (river)">Granta</a> changed their name to match.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>) <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> grave goods have been found in the area. During this period, Cambridge benefited from good trade links across the hard-to-travel fenlands. By the 7th century, the town was less significant and described by <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Bede</a> as a "little ruined city" containing the burial site of <a href="/wiki/Etheldreda" class="mw-redirect" title="Etheldreda">Etheldreda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach2-15_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach2-15-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge was on the border between the <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Anglia" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Anglia">Middle Anglian</a> kingdoms and the settlement slowly expanded on both sides of the river.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach2-15_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach2-15-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Benets_exterior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/St_Benets_exterior.jpg/220px-St_Benets_exterior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/St_Benets_exterior.jpg/330px-St_Benets_exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/St_Benets_exterior.jpg/440px-St_Benets_exterior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Benets_exterior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Bene%27t%27s_Church" title="St Bene&#39;t&#39;s Church">St Bene't's Church</a>, the oldest standing building in Cambridgeshire, situated next to <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College,_Cambridge" title="Corpus Christi College, Cambridge">Corpus Christi College</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> was recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> in 875. Viking rule, the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a>, had been imposed by 878<sup id="cite_ref-Brooke_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooke-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Their vigorous trading habits caused the town to grow rapidly. During this period the centre of the town shifted from Castle Hill on the left bank of the river to the area now known as the Quayside on the right bank.<sup id="cite_ref-Brooke_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooke-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> After the Viking period, the Saxons enjoyed a return to power, building churches such as <a href="/wiki/St_Bene%27t%27s_Church" title="St Bene&#39;t&#39;s Church">St Bene't's Church</a>, wharves, merchant houses and a <a href="/wiki/Mint_(coin)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mint (coin)">mint</a>, which produced coins with the town's name abbreviated to "Grant".<sup id="cite_ref-Brooke_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooke-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1068, two years after his conquest of England, <a href="/wiki/William_of_Normandy" class="mw-redirect" title="William of Normandy">William of Normandy</a> built a <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Castle" title="Cambridge Castle">castle</a> on Castle Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach2-15_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach2-15-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Like the rest of the newly conquered kingdom, Cambridge fell under the control of the King and his deputies.
</p><p>The first town charter was granted by <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_England" title="Henry I of England">Henry I</a> between 1120 and 1131. It gave Cambridge monopoly of waterborne traffic and hithe tolls and recognised the <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> court.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66606_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66606-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The distinctive <a href="/wiki/The_Holy_Sepulchre,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="The Holy Sepulchre, Cambridge">Round Church</a> dates from this period.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1209, Cambridge University was founded by students escaping from hostile townspeople in <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The oldest existing college, <a href="/wiki/Peterhouse,_Cambridge" title="Peterhouse, Cambridge">Peterhouse</a>, was founded in 1284.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1349 Cambridge was affected by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>. Few records survive but 16 of 40 scholars at <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Hall,_Cambridge" title="King&#39;s Hall, Cambridge">King's Hall</a> died.<sup id="cite_ref-Ziegler_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ziegler-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The town north of the river was severely affected being almost wiped out.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Following further depopulation after a second national epidemic in 1361, a letter from the Bishop of Ely suggested that two parishes in Cambridge be merged as there were not enough people to fill even one church.<sup id="cite_ref-Ziegler_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ziegler-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> With more than a third of English clergy dying in the Black Death, four new colleges were established at the university over the following years to train new clergymen, namely <a href="/wiki/Gonville_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Gonville Hall">Gonville Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Hall,_Cambridge" title="Trinity Hall, Cambridge">Trinity Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College,_Cambridge" title="Corpus Christi College, Cambridge">Corpus Christi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clare_College,_Cambridge" title="Clare College, Cambridge">Clare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1382 a revised town charter effects a "diminution of the liberties that the community had enjoyed", due to Cambridge's participation in the <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants' Revolt</a>. The charter transfers supervision of baking and brewing, weights and measures, and <a href="/wiki/Engrossing_(law)" title="Engrossing (law)">forestalling and regrating</a>, from the town to the university.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66606_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66606-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_Chapel,_Cambridge" title="King&#39;s College Chapel, Cambridge">King's College Chapel</a>, was begun in 1446 by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">King Henry VI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kings_Chapel_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kings_Chapel-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  The chapel was built in phases by a succession of kings of England from 1446 to 1515, its history intertwined with the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>, and completed during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">King Henry VIII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kings_Chapel_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kings_Chapel-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The building would become synonymous with Cambridge, and currently is used in the logo for the City Council.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg/220px-Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg/330px-Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg/440px-Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Part_of_Peterhouse_College_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1508178.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peterhouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Peterhouse">Peterhouse</a> was the first college to be founded in the University of Cambridge.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern">Early modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg/220px-Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg/330px-Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg/440px-Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2656" data-file-height="1984" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_1575_colour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambridge in 1575</div></div></div>
<p>Following repeated outbreaks of pestilence throughout the 16th Century,<sup id="cite_ref-publichealth_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publichealth-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> sanitation and fresh water were brought to Cambridge by the construction of <a href="/wiki/Hobson%27s_Conduit" title="Hobson&#39;s Conduit">Hobson's Conduit</a> in the early 1600s. Water was brought from Nine Wells, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Gog_Magog_Hills" title="Gog Magog Hills">Gog Magog Hills</a>, into the centre of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cambridge played a significant role in the early part of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> as it was the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association" title="Eastern Association">Eastern Counties Association</a>, an organisation administering a regional <a href="/wiki/East_Anglian" class="mw-redirect" title="East Anglian">East Anglian</a> army, which became the mainstay of the Parliamentarian military effort before the formation of the <a href="/wiki/New_Model_Army" title="New Model Army">New Model Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1643 control of the town was given by Parliament to <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>, who had been educated at <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Sussex_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Sidney Sussex College">Sidney Sussex College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The town's castle was fortified and garrisoned with troops and some bridges were destroyed to aid its defence. Although <a href="/wiki/Royalist" title="Royalist">Royalist</a> forces came within 2 miles (3&#160;km) of the town in 1644, the defences were never used and the garrison was stood down the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early-industrial_era">Early-industrial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early-industrial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 19th century, in common with many other English towns, Cambridge expanded rapidly, due in part to increased life expectancy and improved agricultural production leading to increased trade in town markets.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66609_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66609-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inclosure_Acts" title="Inclosure Acts">Inclosure Acts</a> of 1801 and 1807 enabled the town to expand over surrounding open fields and in 1912 and again in 1935 its boundaries were extended to include Chesterton, Cherry Hinton, and Trumpington.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The railway came to Cambridge in 1845 after initial resistance, with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Eastern_Railway" title="Great Eastern Railway">Great Eastern Railway</a>'s London to Norwich line. The station was outside the town centre following pressure from the university to restrict travel by undergraduates.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66603_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66603-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> With the arrival of the railway and associated employment came development of areas around the station, such as <a href="/wiki/Mill_Road,_Cambridge" title="Mill Road, Cambridge">Romsey Town</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brigham_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brigham-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The rail link to London stimulated heavier industries, such as the production of brick, cement and <a href="/wiki/Malt" title="Malt">malt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66609_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66609-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the 1930s to the 1980s, the size of the city was increased by several large <a href="/wiki/Council_estate" class="mw-redirect" title="Council estate">council estates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-15307_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-15307-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The biggest impact has been on the area north of the river, which are now the estates of <a href="/wiki/East_Chesterton" class="mw-redirect" title="East Chesterton">East Chesterton</a>, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Hedges" title="King&#39;s Hedges">King's Hedges</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arbury" title="Arbury">Arbury</a> where <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop</a> <a href="/wiki/Rowan_Williams" title="Rowan Williams">Rowan Williams</a> lived and worked as an assistant priest in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the Second World War, Cambridge was an important centre for defence of the east coast. The town became a military centre, with an <a href="/wiki/R.A.F." class="mw-redirect" title="R.A.F.">R.A.F.</a> training centre and the regional headquarters for Norfolk, Suffolk, Essex, Cambridgeshire, <a href="/wiki/Huntingdonshire" title="Huntingdonshire">Huntingdonshire</a>, Hertfordshire, and <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire" title="Bedfordshire">Bedfordshire</a> established during the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The town itself escaped relatively lightly from German bombing raids, which were mainly targeted at the railway. 29 people were killed and no historic buildings were damaged. In 1944, a secret meeting of military leaders held in Trinity College laid the foundation for the allied invasion of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66609_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66609-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> During the war Cambridge served as an <a href="/wiki/Evacuations_of_civilians_in_Britain_during_World_War_II" title="Evacuations of civilians in Britain during World War II">evacuation centre</a> for over 7,000 people from London, as well as for parts of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cambridge was granted its <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city charter</a> in 1951 in recognition of its history, administrative importance and economic success.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66605_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66605-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge does not have a cathedral, traditionally a prerequisite for city status, instead falling within the Church of England <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Ely" title="Diocese of Ely">Diocese of Ely</a>. In 1962 Cambridge's first shopping arcade, Bradwell's Court, opened on Drummer Street, though this was demolished in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Other shopping arcades followed at Lion Yard, which housed a relocated Central Library for the city, and the <a href="/wiki/Grafton_Centre" title="Grafton Centre">Grafton Centre</a> which replaced Victorian housing stock which had fallen into disrepair in <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Kite,_Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Kite, Cambridge (page does not exist)">the Kite area</a> of the city. This latter project was controversial at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city gained its second University in 1992 when Anglia Polytechnic became Anglia Polytechnic University. Renamed <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a> in 2005, the institution has its origins in the Cambridge School of Art opened in 1858 by <a href="/wiki/John_Ruskin" title="John Ruskin">John Ruskin</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Open_University" class="mw-redirect" title="The Open University">The Open University</a> also has a presence in the city, with an office operating on Hills Road.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg/300px-Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg/450px-Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg/600px-Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_UK_ward_map_2010_coloured_on_Cambridge-Openstreetmap-08-06-13.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the 2010 electoral boundaries of the city, with <a href="/wiki/Postcode_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Postcode district">postcode districts</a> superimposed.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_local_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge local elections">Cambridge local elections</a></div>
<p>Cambridge is a <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district" title="Non-metropolitan district">non-metropolitan district</a> served by <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_City_Council" title="Cambridge City Council">Cambridge City Council</a>. Cambridge Local Authority District covers most of the City's urban area but some extends outside this into South Cambridgeshire District. Cambridge is one of five districts within the county of Cambridgeshire, and is bordered on all sides by the mainly rural <a href="/wiki/South_Cambridgeshire" title="South Cambridgeshire">South Cambridgeshire</a> district. The city council's headquarters are in the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Guildhall" title="Cambridge Guildhall">Guildhall</a>, a large building in the market square. Cambridge was granted a Royal Charter by King John in 1207, which permitted the appointment of a Mayor,<sup id="cite_ref-1207charter_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1207charter-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> although the first recorded Mayor, Harvey FitzEustace, served in 1213.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> City councillors now elect a mayor annually.
</p><p>For electoral purposes the city is divided into 14 wards: Abbey, <a href="/wiki/Arbury" title="Arbury">Arbury</a>, Castle, <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hinton" title="Cherry Hinton">Cherry Hinton</a>, Coleridge, <a href="/wiki/Chesterton,_Cambridge" title="Chesterton, Cambridge">East Chesterton</a>, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Hedges" title="King&#39;s Hedges">King's Hedges</a>, Market, <a href="/wiki/Newnham,_Cambridgeshire" title="Newnham, Cambridgeshire">Newnham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mill_Road,_Cambridge" title="Mill Road, Cambridge">Petersfield</a>, Queen Edith's, <a href="/wiki/Mill_Road,_Cambridge" title="Mill Road, Cambridge">Romsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trumpington,_Cambridgeshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Trumpington, Cambridgeshire">Trumpington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chesterton,_Cambridge" title="Chesterton, Cambridge">West Chesterton</a>. The political composition of the city council is currently:  25 <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> councillors, 14 <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a>, 2 independent  and one <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each of the 14 wards also elects councillors to <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_County_Council" title="Cambridgeshire County Council">Cambridgeshire County Council</a>. Responsible for services including school education, social care and highways, since 2017 the County Council has been controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Westminster">Westminster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Westminster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)">Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)">constituency of Cambridge</a> covers most of the city. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Zeichner" title="Daniel Zeichner">Daniel Zeichner</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>) was elected Member of Parliament (MP) at the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 general election</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Julian_Huppert" title="Julian Huppert">Julian Huppert</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a>. He was re-elected in the <a href="/wiki/2017_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2017 United Kingdom general election">2017 general election</a>. One area of the city, Queen Edith's ward,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> lies in the <a href="/wiki/South_Cambridgeshire_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="South Cambridgeshire (UK Parliament constituency)">South Cambridgeshire</a> constituency, whose MP is <a href="/wiki/Heidi_Allen" title="Heidi Allen">Heidi Allen</a> (Independent).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Allen was also elected in 2015, succeeding <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lansley" title="Andrew Lansley">Andrew Lansley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and was re-elected in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The city had previously elected a Labour MP from 1992 to 2005 and prior to this, usually elected a Conservative after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">the Second World War</a>. However, the Conservatives have seen their share of the vote fall over the past 20 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The University of Cambridge formerly had two seats in the House of Commons; <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Sir Isaac Newton</a> was one of the most notable MPs. The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge University (UK Parliament constituency)">Cambridge University constituency</a> was abolished under 1948 legislation, and ceased at the dissolution of Parliament for the <a href="/wiki/1950_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1950 United Kingdom general election">1950 general election</a>, along with the other <a href="/wiki/University_constituency" title="University constituency">university constituencies</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_environment">Geography and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Places_adjacent_to_Cambridge" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks mw-collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Adjacent_communities" title="Template:Adjacent communities"><abbr title="View this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Adjacent_communities" title="Template talk:Adjacent communities"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Adjacent_communities&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div><div id="Places_adjacent_to_Cambridge" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">Places adjacent to Cambridge</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin:0; text-align:center;"><tbody><tr>

<p>Cambridge is situated about 50 miles (80&#160;km) north-by-east of London. The city is located in an area of level and relatively low-lying terrain just south of <a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">the Fens</a>, which varies between 6 and 24 metres (20 and 79&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-http&#58;//www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/90641/Cambridge_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/90641/Cambridge-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The town was thus historically surrounded by low lying wetlands that have been drained as the town has expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The underlying geology of Cambridge consists of <a href="/wiki/Gault" title="Gault">gault</a> clay and <a href="/wiki/Chalk_Group" title="Chalk Group">Chalk Marl</a>, known locally as Cambridge Greensand,<sup id="cite_ref-NatEngGeo_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatEngGeo-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> partly overlaid by <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">terrace gravel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A layer of <a href="/wiki/Phosphate_nodule" class="mw-redirect" title="Phosphate nodule">phosphatic nodules</a> (<a href="/wiki/Coprolites" class="mw-redirect" title="Coprolites">coprolites</a>) under the marl were mined in the 19th century for fertiliser. It became a major industry in the county, and its profits yielded buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Corn_Exchange" title="Cambridge Corn Exchange">Corn Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulbourn_Hospital" title="Fulbourn Hospital">Fulbourn Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_College,_Cambridge#College_Chapel" title="St John&#39;s College, Cambridge">St. John's Chapel</a> until the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Acts_of_the_Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom,_1880%E2%80%931899#1894" title="List of Acts of the Parliament of the United Kingdom, 1880–1899">Quarries Act 1894</a> and competition from America ended production.<sup id="cite_ref-NatEngGeo_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatEngGeo-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/River_Cam" title="River Cam">River Cam</a> flows through the city from the village of <a href="/wiki/Grantchester" title="Grantchester">Grantchester</a>, to the southwest. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Water_meadows" class="mw-redirect" title="Water meadows">water meadows</a> within the city such as <a href="/wiki/Sheep%27s_Green" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheep&#39;s Green">Sheep's Green</a> as well as residential development.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Like most cities, modern-day Cambridge has many suburbs and areas of high-density housing. The city centre of Cambridge is mostly commercial, historic buildings, and large green areas such as Jesus Green, <a href="/wiki/Parker%27s_Piece" title="Parker&#39;s Piece">Parker's Piece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midsummer_Common" title="Midsummer Common">Midsummer Common</a>. Many of the roads in the centre are pedestrianised. Population growth has seen new housing developments in the 21st century, with estates such as the CB1<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Accordia" title="Accordia">Accordia</a> schemes near the station,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and developments such as <a href="/wiki/Great_Kneighton" title="Great Kneighton">Great Kneighton</a>, formally known as Clay Farm,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and Trumpington Meadows<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> currently under construction in the south of the city. Other major developments currently being constructed in the city are Darwin Green (formerly <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Agricultural_Botany" title="National Institute of Agricultural Botany">NIAB</a>), and University-led developments at <a href="/wiki/West_Cambridge" title="West Cambridge">West Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_West_Cambridge_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="North West Cambridge Development">North West Cambridge</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Eddington,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Eddington, Cambridge">Eddington</a>).
</p><p>The entire city centre, as well as parts of Chesterton, Petersfield, West Cambridge, Newnham, and Abbey, are covered by an <a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Quality_Management_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Air Quality Management Area (page does not exist)">Air Quality Management Area</a>, implemented to counter high levels of <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide" title="Nitrogen dioxide">nitrogen dioxide</a> in the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>. (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: <i>Cfb</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge currently has two official weather observing stations, the National Institute of Agricultural Botany (NIAB), about 1 mile (2&#160;km) north of the city boundary near <a href="/wiki/Histon" class="mw-redirect" title="Histon">Histon</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Botanic_Garden" title="Cambridge University Botanic Garden">Cambridge University Botanic Garden</a>, about 1 mile south of the city centre. In addition, the Digital Technology Group of the University's <a href="/wiki/Computer_Laboratory,_University_of_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer Laboratory, University of Cambridge">Computer Laboratory</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> maintains a weather station on the <a href="/wiki/West_Cambridge" title="West Cambridge">West Cambridge site</a>, displaying current weather conditions online via web browsers or an <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">app</a>, and also an archive dating back to 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city, like most of the UK, has a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a> highly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. Located in the driest region of Britain,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge's rainfall averages around 570&#160;mm (22.44&#160;in) per year, around half the national average,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> with some years occasionally falling into the semi-arid (under 500&#160;mm (19.69&#160;in) of rain per year) category. The last time this occurred was in 2011 with 380.4&#160;mm (14.98&#160;in)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> of rain at the Botanic Garden and 347.2&#160;mm (13.67&#160;in) at the NIAB site.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Conversely, 2012 was the wettest year on record, with 812.7&#160;mm (32.00&#160;in) reported.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Snowfall accumulations are usually small, in part because of Cambridge's low elevation, and low precipitation tendency during transitional snow events.
</p><p>Owing to its low lying, inland, and easterly position within the British Isles, summer temperatures tend to be somewhat higher than areas further west, and often rival or even exceed those recorded in the London area. July 2006 for example recorded the highest official mean monthly maximum (i.e. averaged over the entire month) of any month at any location in the UK since records began; 28.3&#160;°C (82.9&#160;°F), at both the NIAB<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and Botanic Garden<sup id="cite_ref-ECAD-July2006_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECAD-July2006-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> observing stations.  Cambridge also often records the annual highest national temperature in any given year&#160;– 30.2&#160;°C (86.4&#160;°F) in July 2008 at NIAB<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and 30.1&#160;°C (86.2&#160;°F) in August 2007 at the Botanic Garden<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> are two recent examples. The absolute maximum stands at 38.7&#160;°C (101.7&#160;°F) recorded on 25 July 2019 at Cambridge University Botanic Garden,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> which is also the national all time temperature record. Typically the temperature will reach 25.1&#160;°C (77.2&#160;°F) or higher on over 25 days of the year over the 1981–2010 period,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> with the annual warmest day averaging 31.5&#160;°C (88.7&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> over the same period.
</p><p>The absolute minimum temperature recorded at the Botanic Garden site was −17.2&#160;°C (1.0&#160;°F), recorded in February 1947,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> although a minimum of −17.8&#160;°C (0.0&#160;°F) was recorded at the now defunct observatory site in December 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> More recently the temperature fell to −15.3&#160;°C (4.5&#160;°F) on 11 February 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> −12.2&#160;°C (10.0&#160;°F) on 22 January 2013<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and −10.9&#160;°C (12.4&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> on 20 December 2010. The average frequency of air frosts ranges from 42.8 days at the NIAB site,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> to 48.3 days at the Botanic Garden<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> per year over the 1981–2010 period. Typically the coldest night of the year at the Botanic Garden will fall to −8.0&#160;°C (17.6&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Such minimum temperatures and frost averages are typical for inland areas across much of southern and central England.
</p><p>Sunshine averages around 1,500 hours a year or around 35% of possible, a level typical of most locations in inland central England.
</p>

<p><br />
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city contains three <a href="/wiki/Site_of_Special_Scientific_Interest" title="Site of Special Scientific Interest">Sites of Special Scientific Interest</a> (SSSIs), at Cherry Hinton East Pit, Cherry Hinton West Pit, and Travellers Pit,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and ten <a href="/wiki/Local_nature_reserve" title="Local nature reserve">Local Nature Reserves</a> (LNRs): Sheep's Green and Coe Fen,
Coldhams Common, Stourbridge Common, Nine Wells, Byron's Pool, West Pit, Paradise, Barnwell West, Barnwell East, and Logan's Meadow.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Green_Belt" title="Cambridge Green Belt">Cambridge Green Belt</a></div>
<p>Cambridge is completely enclosed by <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> as a part of a wider environmental and planning policy first defined in 1965 and formalised in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Cambridge-Green-Belt_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cambridge-Green-Belt-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> While some small tracts of green belt exist on the fringes of the city's boundary, much of the protection is in the surrounding South Cambridgeshire<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and nearby <a href="/wiki/East_Cambridgeshire" title="East Cambridgeshire">East Cambridgeshire</a><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> districts, helping to maintain local green space, prevent further <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a> and unplanned expansion of the city, as well as protecting smaller outlying villages from further convergence with each other as well as the city.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The demography in Cambridge changes considerably in and out of University term times, so can be hard to measure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">2001 Census</a> held during University term, 89.44% of Cambridge residents identified themselves as white, compared with a national average of 92.12%.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Within the University, 84% of undergraduates and 80% of post-graduates identify as white (including overseas students).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cambridge has a much higher than average proportion of people in the highest paid professional, managerial or administrative jobs (32.6% vs. 23.5%)<sup id="cite_ref-2001CensusASG_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001CensusASG-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and a much lower than average proportion of manual workers (27.6% vs. 40.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-2001CensusASG_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001CensusASG-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In addition, a much higher than average proportion of people have a high level qualification (e.g. degree, <a href="/wiki/Higher_National_Diploma" title="Higher National Diploma">Higher National Diploma</a>, Master's or PhD), (41.2% vs. 19.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Cities" title="Centre for Cities">Centre for Cities</a> identified Cambridge as the UK's most unequal city in 2017 and 2018. Residents' income was the least evenly distributed of 57 British cities measured, with its top 6% earners accounting for 19% of its total income and the bottom 20% for only 2%, and a <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> of 0.460 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
