<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The town's river link to the surrounding agricultural land, and good road connections to London in the south meant Cambridge has historically served as an important regional trading post. King Henry I granted Cambridge a monopoly on river trade, privileging this area of the economy of Cambridge <sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The town <a href="/wiki/Market_Hill,_Cambridge" title="Market Hill, Cambridge">market</a> provided for trade in a wide variety of goods and annual trading fairs such as <a href="/wiki/Stourbridge_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Stourbridge Fair">Stourbridge Fair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midsummer_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Midsummer Fair">Midsummer Fair</a> were visited by merchants from across the country. The river was described in an account of 1748 as being "often so full of [merchant boats] that the navigation thereof is stopped for some time".<sup id="cite_ref-Gentleman1748_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gentleman1748-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> For example, 2000 <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/firkin" class="extiw" title="wikt:Special:Search/firkin">firkins</a> of butter were brought up the river every Monday from the agricultural lands to the North East, particularity Norfolk, to be unloaded in the town for road transportation to London.<sup id="cite_ref-Gentleman1748_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gentleman1748-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Changing patterns of retail distribution and the advent of the railways led to a decline in Cambridge's importance as a market town.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg/250px-S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg/375px-S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg/500px-S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:S95MarketCambridgefromGreatStMarys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambridge Market viewed from the Tower of <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Mary_the_Great,_Cambridge" title="Church of St Mary the Great, Cambridge">St. Mary the Great</a></div></div></div>
<p>Today Cambridge has a diverse economy with strength in sectors such as research &amp; development, software consultancy, high value engineering, creative industries, pharmaceuticals and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Described as one of the "most beautiful cities in the world" by <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> with the view from <a href="/wiki/The_Backs" title="The Backs">The Backs</a> being selected as one of the 10 greatest in England by <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust</a> chair <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jenkins" title="Simon Jenkins">Simon Jenkins</a>, tourism generates over £750 million for the city's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cambridge and its surrounds are sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Fen" title="Silicon Fen">Silicon Fen</a>, an allusion to <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>, because of the density of high-tech businesses and <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">technology incubators</a> that have developed on <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a> around the city. Many of these parks and buildings are owned or leased by university colleges, and the companies often have been spun out of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Science_Park" title="Cambridge Science Park">Cambridge Science Park</a>, which is the largest commercial R&amp;D centre in Europe, is owned by <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity College Cambridge">Trinity College</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="St John&#39;s College, Cambridge">St John's</a> is the landlord of <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_Innovation_Centre" title="St John&#39;s Innovation Centre">St John's Innovation Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Technology companies include <a href="/wiki/Abcam_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Abcam plc">Abcam</a>, <a href="/wiki/CSR_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="CSR plc">CSR</a>, <a href="/wiki/ARM_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="ARM Limited">ARM Limited</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Semiconductor_Limited" title="Cambridge Semiconductor Limited">CamSemi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jagex" title="Jagex">Jagex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Research_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinclair Research Ltd">Sinclair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> has located its <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Research" title="Microsoft Research">Microsoft Research</a> UK offices in <a href="/wiki/West_Cambridge" title="West Cambridge">West Cambridge</a>, separate from the main Microsoft UK campus in <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>, and also has an office on Station Road.
</p><p>Cambridge was also the home of <a href="/wiki/Pye_Ltd." title="Pye Ltd.">Pye Ltd.</a>, founded in 1898 by W. G. Pye, who worked in the <a href="/wiki/Cavendish_Laboratory" title="Cavendish Laboratory">Cavendish Laboratory</a>; it began by supplying the University and later specialised in wireless telegraphy equipment, radios, televisions and also defence equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history-66609_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history-66609-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Pye Ltd evolved into several other companies including <a href="/wiki/TETRA" class="mw-redirect" title="TETRA">TETRA</a> radio equipment manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Sepura" title="Sepura">Sepura</a>. Another major business is <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall Aerospace">Marshall Aerospace</a> located on the eastern edge of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Network" title="Cambridge Network">Cambridge Network</a> keeps businesses in touch with each other. The software company <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Corporation">Autonomy Corporation</a> is located at the Business Park on Cowley Road.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cambridge" title="Transport in Cambridge">Transport in Cambridge</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg/220px-Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg/330px-Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg/440px-Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_from_Trumpington_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2543891.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A guided bus on the Cambridgeshire Guided Busway</div></div></div>
<p>Because of its rapid growth in the 20th century, Cambridge has a congested road network.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/M11_motorway" title="M11 motorway">M11 motorway</a> from east London terminates to the north-west of the city where it joins the <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14</a>, a major freight route which connects the port of <a href="/wiki/Felixstowe" title="Felixstowe">Felixstowe</a> on the east coast with the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a>. The A428 connects the city with <a href="/wiki/Bedford,_Bedfordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedford, Bedfordshire">Bedford</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Neots" title="St Neots">St Neots</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/A10_road_(England)" title="A10 road (England)">A10</a> connects the city to <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn" title="King&#39;s Lynn">King's Lynn</a> to the north via <a href="/wiki/Ely,_Cambridgeshire" title="Ely, Cambridgeshire">Ely</a>, and to central London to the south.
</p><p>As a university town lying on fairly flat ground and with traffic congestion, Cambridge has the highest level of cycle use in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2001 census, 25% of residents travelled to work by bicycle. Furthermore, a survey in 2013 found that 47% of residents travel by bike at least once a week.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In recognition of this, the 3rd stage of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Tour_de_France" title="2014 Tour de France">2014 Tour de France</a> started in the city, adjacent to Parker's Piece.
</p><p>Cambridge has several bus services including routes linking five <a href="/wiki/Park_and_Ride" class="mw-redirect" title="Park and Ride">Park and Ride</a> sites all of which operate seven days a week and are aimed at encouraging motorists to park near the city's edge.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Since 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway" title="Cambridgeshire Guided Busway">Cambridgeshire Guided Busway</a> has carried bus services into the centre of Cambridge from <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cambridgeshire" title="St Ives, Cambridgeshire">St Ives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon" title="Huntingdon">Huntingdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> and other towns and villages along the routes, operated by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_in_The_Fens" title="Stagecoach in The Fens">Stagecoach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Go_Whippet" title="Go Whippet">Go Whippet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The A service continues on to the railway station and <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrookes</a>, before terminating at a new Park and Ride in <a href="/wiki/Trumpington,_Cambridgeshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Trumpington, Cambridgeshire">Trumpington</a>. Since 2017 it has also linked to Cambridge North railway station.
</p><p>Cambridge also has its own airport; <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Airport">Cambridge Airport</a> was used mainly by charter and training flights as well as to fly in aircraft for maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Regular flights to <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> and European destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> operated until the end of January 2016 when all scheduled and charter traffic from the airport was halted.<sup id="cite_ref-cn2dec15_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn2dec15-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a> was opened in 1845, initially linking to <a href="/wiki/Bishopsgate_railway_station" title="Bishopsgate railway station">Bishopsgate station</a> in London, via Bishops Stortford.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Further lines opened throughout the 19th century, including the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_and_St_Ives_branch_line" title="Cambridge and St Ives branch line">Cambridge and St Ives branch line</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stour_Valley_Railway" title="Stour Valley Railway">Stour Valley Railway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_to_Mildenhall_railway" title="Cambridge to Mildenhall railway">Cambridge to Mildenhall railway</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Line" title="Varsity Line">Varsity Line</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cherryhinton_railway_station" title="Cherryhinton railway station">Another station</a> was opened in Cherry Hinton though, at the time, this was a separate village to Cambridge. Several of these lines were closed during the 1960s.
</p><p>Today, Cambridge station has direct rail links to London with termini at <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a> (via the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Line">Cambridge Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>), <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Street railway station">Liverpool Street</a> (on the <a href="/wiki/West_Anglia_Main_Line" title="West Anglia Main Line">West Anglia Main Line</a>), and <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras</a> (on the <a href="/wiki/Thameslink" title="Thameslink">Thameslink</a> line). Commuter trains to King's Cross run every half hour during peak hours, with a journey time of 53 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Trains also run to <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn_railway_station" title="King&#39;s Lynn railway station">King's Lynn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ely_railway_station" title="Ely railway station">Ely</a> (via the <a href="/wiki/Fen_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Fen Line">Fen Line</a>), <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> (via the <a href="/wiki/Breckland_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Breckland Line">Breckland Line</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_railway_station" title="Peterborough railway station">Peterborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevenage_railway_station" title="Stevenage railway station">Stevenage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_railway_station" title="Ipswich railway station">Ipswich</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brighton_railway_station" title="Brighton railway station">Brighton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport</a>.
</p><p>A second railway station, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_North_railway_station" title="Cambridge North railway station">Cambridge North</a>, opened on 21 May 2017, having originally planned to open in March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-February_2012_Cambridge_News_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-February_2012_Cambridge_News-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> A third railway station, Cambridge South, near Addenbrooke's Hospital has been proposed.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main,_28_Sep,_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg/330px-Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg/440px-Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main%2C_28_Sep%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2925" data-file-height="1950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anglia_Ruskin_Cambridge_Main,_28_Sep,_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a> evolved from the nineteenth century Cambridge School of Art, opened by <a href="/wiki/Educationist" class="mw-redirect" title="Educationist">educationist</a> and art figure <a href="/wiki/John_Ruskin" title="John Ruskin">John Ruskin</a> in 1858</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Cambridgeshire" title="List of schools in Cambridgeshire">List of schools in Cambridgeshire</a></div>
<p>Cambridge's two universities,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> the collegiate <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> and the local campus of <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a>, serve around 30,000 students, by some estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge University estimated its 2007/08 student population at 17,662,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and Anglia Ruskin reports 24,000 students across its two campuses (one of which is outside Cambridge, in <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford,_Essex" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelmsford, Essex">Chelmsford</a>) for the same period. <sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> ARU now (2019) has additional campuses in London and Perborough. State provision in the <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> sector includes <a href="/wiki/Hills_Road_Sixth_Form_College" title="Hills Road Sixth Form College">Hills Road Sixth Form College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Road_Sixth_Form_College" title="Long Road Sixth Form College">Long Road Sixth Form College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Regional_College" title="Cambridge Regional College">Cambridge Regional College</a>.
</p><p>Both state and <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent school (UK)">independent schools</a> serve Cambridge pupils from nursery to secondary school age. State schools are administered by Cambridgeshire County Council, which maintains 251 schools in total,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> 35 of them in Cambridge city.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Netherhall_School" title="Netherhall School">Netherhall School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chesterton_Community_College" title="Chesterton Community College">Chesterton Community College</a>, the Parkside Federation (comprising <a href="/wiki/Parkside_Community_College" title="Parkside Community College">Parkside Community College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coleridge_Community_College" title="Coleridge Community College">Coleridge Community College</a>), <a href="/wiki/North_Cambridge_Academy" title="North Cambridge Academy">North Cambridge Academy</a> and the Christian inter-denominational <a href="/wiki/St_Bede%27s_Inter-Church_School" title="St Bede&#39;s Inter-Church School">St Bede's School</a> provide <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">comprehensive</a> secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Many other pupils from the Cambridge area attend <a href="/wiki/Village_college" title="Village college">village colleges</a>, an educational institution unique to Cambridgeshire, which serve as secondary schools during the day and adult education centres outside of school hours.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Independent schools in the city include <a href="/wiki/The_Perse_School" title="The Perse School">The Perse School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Perse_Foundation" title="Stephen Perse Foundation">Stephen Perse Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sancton_Wood_School" title="Sancton Wood School">Sancton Wood School</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_School,_Cambridge" title="St Mary&#39;s School, Cambridge">St Mary's School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heritage_School,_Cambridge" title="Heritage School, Cambridge">Heritage School</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Leys_School" title="The Leys School">The Leys School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The city has one <a href="/wiki/University_Technical_College" class="mw-redirect" title="University Technical College">university technical college</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Academy_for_Science_and_Technology" title="Cambridge Academy for Science and Technology">Cambridge Academy for Science and Technology</a>, which opened in September 2014.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg/220px-Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg/330px-Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg/440px-Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reality_Checkpoint_-_geograph.org.uk_-_971592.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parker's Piece</div></div></div>
<p>Cambridge played a unique role in the invention of modern <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>: the game's first set of rules were drawn up by members of the University in 1848. The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Rules">Cambridge Rules</a> were first played on <a href="/wiki/Parker%27s_Piece" title="Parker&#39;s Piece">Parker's Piece</a> and had a 'defining influence on the 1863 <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a> rules' which again were first played on Parker's Piece.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is home to <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_United_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge United FC">Cambridge United FC</a>, who play at the <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Stadium" title="Abbey Stadium">Abbey Stadium</a>. Formed in 1912, as Abbey United, they were elected to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> in 1970 and reached the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Football League Second Division</a> in 1978, although a serious decline in them in the mid 1980s saw them drop back down to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Football League Fourth Division</a> and almost go out of business. Success returned to the club in the early 1990s when they won two successive promotions and reached the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> quarter finals in both of those seasons, and in 1992 they came close to becoming the first English team to win three successive Football League promotions which would have taken them into the newly created <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>. But they were beaten in the playoffs and another decline set in, which was completed in 2005 when they were relegated from the Football League and for the second time in 20 years narrowly avoided going out of business. After nine years of non league football they returned to the Football League in 2014 by winning the <a href="/wiki/Conference_National" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference National">Conference National</a> playoffs.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_City_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge City FC">Cambridge City FC</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League_Premier_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Football League Premier Division">Southern Football League Premier Division</a> now play in the adjoining village of <a href="/wiki/Histon_and_Impington" title="Histon and Impington">Histon</a>. Formed in Cambridge in 1908 as Cambridge Town, the club were <a href="/wiki/Southern_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Premier League">Southern Premier League</a> champions in 1962-63, the highest they have finished in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_pyramid" class="mw-redirect" title="English football pyramid">English football pyramid</a>. After a legal dispute with their landlords,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> the club left their home ground in Cambridge in order to <a href="/wiki/Groundshare" title="Groundshare">groundshare</a> with fellow Southern League Premier club  <a href="/wiki/Histon_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Histon FC">Histon FC</a> in 2013-14 and intend to construct a new ground outside the city, in <a href="/wiki/Sawston" title="Sawston">Sawston</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As well as being the home of the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Rules">Cambridge Rules</a> in football, Parker's Piece was used for <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> matches from 1817 to 1864.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The University of Cambridge's cricket ground, <a href="/wiki/Fenner%27s" title="Fenner&#39;s">Fenner's</a>, is located in the city and is one of the home grounds for <a href="/wiki/Minor_counties" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor counties">minor counties</a> team <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_CCC" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridgeshire CCC">Cambridgeshire CCC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> There are seven amateur cricket clubs within the city: Cambridge Granta, Camden, Cambridge St Giles, New Chesterton Institute, Fen Ditton, Romsey Town and Cherry Hinton.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby">Rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is represented in both codes of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby football</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Union">Rugby Union</a> club <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_R.U.F.C." title="Cambridge R.U.F.C.">Cambridge R.U.F.C.</a> were founded in 1923,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and play in <a href="/wiki/National_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="National League One">National League One</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> at their home ground, <a href="/wiki/Grantchester_Road" title="Grantchester Road">Grantchester Road</a>, in the southwest corner of the city. Cambridge Lions represent the city in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, and are members of <a href="/wiki/East_Men%27s_League" class="mw-redirect" title="East Men&#39;s League">East Rugby League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Watersports">Watersports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Watersports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_MayBump2015_(pixinn.net).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/220px-Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/330px-Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/440px-Cambridge_MayBump2015_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4522" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_MayBump2015_(pixinn.net).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bumps_race" title="Bumps race">Bumps race</a> on the <a href="/wiki/River_Cam" title="River Cam">River Cam</a></div></div></div>
<p>The River Cam running through the city centre is used for boating. The University and its colleges are well known for <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_Rowing_Association" title="Cambridgeshire Rowing Association">Cambridgeshire Rowing Association</a>, formed in 1868, organises competitive rowing on the river outside of the University.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Rowing clubs based in the city include <a href="/wiki/City_of_Cambridge_Rowing_Club" title="City of Cambridge Rowing Club">City of Cambridge RC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_%2799_Rowing_Club" title="Cambridge &#39;99 Rowing Club">Cambridge '99 RC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantabrigian_Rowing_Club" title="Cantabrigian Rowing Club">Cantabrigian RC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Roy_Boat_Club" title="Rob Roy Boat Club">Rob Roy BC</a>. Shallower parts of the Cam are used for recreational <a href="/wiki/Punt_(boat)" title="Punt (boat)">punting</a>, a type of boating in which the craft is propelled by pushing against the river bed with a <a href="/wiki/Quant_pole" title="Quant pole">quant pole</a>.
</p><p>Cambridge Swimming Club, Cambridge Dive team, and City of Cambridge Water Polo Club are all based at Parkside Swimming Pool.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greyhound_racing">Greyhound racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Greyhound racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are three known former venues for <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_racing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Greyhound racing in the United Kingdom">greyhound racing</a> in Cambridge. The most significant venue was the racing held around the <a href="/wiki/City_Ground_(Cambridge)" title="City Ground (Cambridge)">City Ground</a> which was licensed by the sports governing body the <a href="/wiki/National_Greyhound_Racing_Club" title="National Greyhound Racing Club">National Greyhound Racing Club</a> (NGRC) and took place from 1968 to 1984. The other two venues were independent tracks and known as a flapping tracks, the nickname given to non-NGRC tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> They were at Coldham Road, which was opened by the Cambridge and District Greyhound Racing Club on 10 April 1931, and Cowper Lane which also opened in 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambridge is home to two <a href="/wiki/Real_Tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Tennis">Real Tennis</a> courts (out of just 42 in the world) at Cambridge University Real Tennis Club.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_American_Football_League" title="British American Football League">British American Football League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_Cats" title="Cambridgeshire Cats">Cambridgeshire Cats</a> play at Coldham's Common. Cambridge Royals are members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Baseball_Federation" title="British Baseball Federation">British Baseball Federation</a>'s Triple-A South Division.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge has two cycling clubs: Team Cambridge<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and Cambridge Cycling Club.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_%26_Coleridge_Athletic_Club" title="Cambridge &amp; Coleridge Athletic Club">Cambridge &amp; Coleridge Athletic Club</a><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> is the city's track and field club, based at the University of Cambridge's Wilberforce Road track. Cambridge <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">Handball</a> Club compete in the men's England Handball National Super 8 League, and the women's England Handball National Super 7 League. There are three field hockey clubs; <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_City_Hockey_Club" title="Cambridge City Hockey Club">Cambridge City Hockey Club</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_South_Hockey_Club" title="Cambridge South Hockey Club">Cambridge South Hockey Club</a> and Cambridge Nomads. 
The city is also represented in <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a> by Cambridge Polo Club, based in <a href="/wiki/Barton,_Cambridgeshire" title="Barton, Cambridgeshire">Barton</a>, just outside the city. The Romsey Town Rollerbillies play <a href="/wiki/Roller_derby" title="Roller derby">roller derby</a> in Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Speedway_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Speedway in the United Kingdom">Speedway</a> racing was formerly staged at a greyhound stadium in Coldhams Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Varsity_sports">Varsity sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Varsity sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambridge is also known for the sporting events between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, especially the rugby union <a href="/wiki/The_Varsity_Match" title="The Varsity Match">Varsity Match</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_and_Cambridge_Boat_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford and Cambridge Boat Race">Boat Race</a>, though many of these do not take place within Cambridge.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CambridgeCorn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/CambridgeCorn.jpg/170px-CambridgeCorn.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/CambridgeCorn.jpg/255px-CambridgeCorn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/CambridgeCorn.jpg/340px-CambridgeCorn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CambridgeCorn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambridge Corn Exchange</div></div></div>
<p>Cambridge's main traditional theatre is the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Arts_Theatre" title="Cambridge Arts Theatre">Arts Theatre</a>, a venue with 666 seats in the town centre.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The theatre often has touring shows, as well as those by local companies. The largest venue in the city to regular hold theatrical performances is the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Corn_Exchange" title="Cambridge Corn Exchange">Cambridge Corn Exchange</a> with a capacity of 1,800 standing or 1,200 seated. Housed within the city's 19th century former <a href="/wiki/Corn_exchange" title="Corn exchange">corn exchange</a> building the venue was used for a variety of additional functions throughout the 20th century including <a href="/wiki/Tea_party_(social_gathering)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tea party (social gathering)">tea parties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor show">motor shows</a>, sports matches and a music venue with temporary stage.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornexhist_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornexhist-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The City Council renovated the building in the 1980s, turning it into a full-time arts venue, hosting theatre, dance and music performances.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornexhist_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornexhist-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
The newest theatre venue in Cambridge is the 220-seat J2, part of <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Junction" title="Cambridge Junction">Cambridge Junction</a> in Cambridge Leisure Park. The venue was opened in 2005 and hosts theatre, dance, live music and comedy<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/ADC_Theatre" title="ADC Theatre">ADC Theatre</a> is managed by the University of Cambridge, and typically has 3 shows a week during term time. It hosts the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Footlights_Dramatic_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University Footlights Dramatic Club">Cambridge University Footlights Dramatic Club</a> which has produced many notable figures in British comedy. The Mumford Theatre is part of <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a>, and hosts shows by both student and non-student groups. There are also a number of venues within the colleges.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Within the city there are several notable museums, some run by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge_Museums" title="University of Cambridge Museums">University of Cambridge Museums</a> consortium and others independent of it.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fitzwilliam_Museum" title="Fitzwilliam Museum">Fitzwilliam Museum</a> is the city's largest, and is the lead museum of the University of Cambridge Museums. Founded in 1816 from the bequeathment and collections of <a href="/wiki/Richard_FitzWilliam,_7th_Viscount_FitzWilliam" title="Richard FitzWilliam, 7th Viscount FitzWilliam">Richard, Viscount FitzWilliam</a>, the museum was originally located in the building of the <a href="/wiki/Perse_Grammar_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Perse Grammar School">Perse Grammar School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Free_School_Lane" title="Free School Lane">Free School Lane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitwilliam_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitwilliam-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> After a brief housing in the University of Cambridge library, it moved to its current, purpose-built building on <a href="/wiki/Trumpington_Street" title="Trumpington Street">Trumpington Street</a> in 1848.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitwilliam_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitwilliam-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The museum has five departments: Antiquities; Applied Arts; Coins and Medals; Manuscripts and Printed Books; and Paintings, Drawings and Prints. Other members of the University of Cambridge Museums are the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Archaeology_and_Anthropology,_University_of_Cambridge" title="Museum of Archaeology and Anthropology, University of Cambridge">Museum of Archaeology and Anthropology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Polar_Research_Institute" title="Scott Polar Research Institute">The Polar Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sedgwick_Museum_of_Earth_Sciences" title="Sedgwick Museum of Earth Sciences">The Sedgwick Museum of Earth Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Classical_Archaeology,_Cambridge" title="Museum of Classical Archaeology, Cambridge">Museum of Classical Archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whipple_Museum_of_the_History_of_Science" title="Whipple Museum of the History of Science">The Whipple Museum of the History of Science</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Museum_of_Zoology" title="Cambridge University Museum of Zoology">University Museum of Zoology</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Cambridge" title="Museum of Cambridge">Museum of Cambridge</a>, formerly known as the Cambridge &amp; County Folk Museum, is a <a href="/wiki/Social_history" title="Social history">social history</a> museum located in a former pub on Castle Street.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Centre_for_Computing_History" title="The Centre for Computing History">The Centre for Computing History</a>, a museum dedicated to the story of the <a href="/wiki/Information_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Information age">Information age</a>, moved to Cambridge from <a href="/wiki/Haverhill,_Suffolk" title="Haverhill, Suffolk">Haverhill</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Housed in a former sewage pumping station, the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Museum_of_Technology" title="Cambridge Museum of Technology">Cambridge Museum of Technology</a> has a collection of large exhibits related to the city's <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">industrial heritage</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_music">Popular music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Popular music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> are the most notable band with roots in Cambridge. The band's former songwriter, guitarist and vocalist <a href="/wiki/Syd_Barrett" title="Syd Barrett">Syd Barrett</a> was born and lived in the city, and he and another founding member, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>, went to school together at <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_High_School_for_Boys" title="Cambridgeshire High School for Boys">Cambridgeshire High School for Boys</a>. <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>, the guitarist who replaced Barrett, was also a Cambridge resident and attended the nearby <a href="/wiki/Perse_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Perse School">Perse School</a>. Bands who were formed in Cambridge include <a href="/wiki/Clean_Bandit" title="Clean Bandit">Clean Bandit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cow" title="Henry Cow">Henry Cow</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Movies_(band)" title="The Movies (band)">The Movies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katrina_and_the_Waves" title="Katrina and the Waves">Katrina and the Waves</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Soft_Boys" title="The Soft Boys">The Soft Boys</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ezio_(band)" title="Ezio (band)">Ezio</a><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Broken_Family_Band" title="The Broken Family Band">The Broken Family Band</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Acid_%26_the_Deadbeats" title="Uncle Acid &amp; the Deadbeats">Uncle Acid &amp; the Deadbeats</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and the pop-classical group <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Singers" class="mw-redirect" title="King&#39;s Singers">King's Singers</a>, who were formed at the University.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Solo artist <a href="/wiki/Boo_Hewerdine" title="Boo Hewerdine">Boo Hewerdine</a><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> is from Cambridge, as are <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">drum and bass</a> artists (and brothers) <a href="/wiki/Nu:Tone" title="Nu:Tone">Nu:Tone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logistics_(artist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Logistics (artist)">Logistics</a>. Singers <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Bellamy" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthew Bellamy">Matthew Bellamy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> of the rock band <a href="/wiki/Muse_(band)" title="Muse (band)">Muse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Robinson" title="Tom Robinson">Tom Robinson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Newton-John" title="Olivia Newton-John">Olivia Newton-John</a><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> were born in the city. 2012 <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Prize" title="Mercury Prize">Mercury Prize</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Alt-J" title="Alt-J">Alt-J</a> are based in Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Live music venues hosting popular music in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Corn_Exchange" title="Cambridge Corn Exchange">Cambridge Corn Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Junction" title="Cambridge Junction">Cambridge Junction</a> and the Portland Arms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_art">Contemporary art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Contemporary art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambridge contains the <a href="/wiki/Kettle%27s_Yard" title="Kettle&#39;s Yard">Kettle's Yard</a> gallery and the artist run organisations Aid and Abet, Cambridge Art Salon, and Changing Spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wysing_Arts_Centre" title="Wysing Arts Centre">Wysing Arts Centre</a>, one of the leading research centres for the visual arts in Europe, is associated with the city, though is located several miles west of Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Anglia Ruskin University operates the publicly accessible Ruskin Gallery within the Cambridge School of Art.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Festivals and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Strawberry_Fair_2007,_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg/220px-Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg/330px-Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg/440px-Strawberry_Fair_2007%2C_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Strawberry_Fair_2007,_Cambridge_-_geograph.org.uk_-_460832.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Strawberry Fair</div></div></div>
<p>Several fairs and festivals take place in Cambridge, mostly during the British summer. <a href="/wiki/Midsummer_Common" title="Midsummer Common">Midsummer Fair</a> dates back to 1211, when it was granted a charter by <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">King John</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Today it exists primarily as an annual <a href="/wiki/Travelling_funfair" class="mw-redirect" title="Travelling funfair">funfair</a> with the vestige of a market attached and is held over several days around or close to <a href="/wiki/Midsummers_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Midsummers day">midsummers day</a>. On the first Saturday in June Midsummer Common is the site for <a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fair" title="Strawberry Fair">Strawberry Fair</a>, a free music and children's fair, with various market stalls. For one week in May, on <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Green" title="Jesus Green">Jesus Green</a>, the annual <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Beer_Festival" title="Cambridge Beer Festival">Cambridge Beer Festival</a> has been held since 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Folk_Festival" title="Cambridge Folk Festival">Cambridge Folk Festival</a> is held annually in the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hinton_Hall" title="Cherry Hinton Hall">Cherry Hinton Hall</a>. The festival has been organised by the city council since its inception in 1964. The Cambridge Summer Music Festival is an annual festival of classical music, held in the University's colleges and chapels.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Shakespeare_Festival" title="Cambridge Shakespeare Festival">Cambridge Shakespeare Festival</a> is an eight-week season of open-air performances of the works of <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, held in the gardens of various colleges of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Started in 1977, the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Film_Festival" title="Cambridge Film Festival">Cambridge Film Festival</a> was held annually in July, moving to September in 2008 to avoid a clash with the rescheduled <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Film Festival">Edinburgh Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Science_Festival" title="Cambridge Science Festival">Cambridge Science Festival</a>, typically held annually in March, is the United Kingdom's largest free <a href="/wiki/Science_festival" title="Science festival">science festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Between 1975 and 1985 the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Poetry_Festival" title="Cambridge Poetry Festival">Cambridge Poetry Festival</a> was held biannually.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Other festivals include the annual Mill Road Winter Fair, held the first Saturday of December,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> the E-luminate Festival, which has taken place every November since 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and The Big Weekend, is a city outdoor event organised by the City Council every July.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_film">Literature and film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature and film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge_in_popular_culture" title="University of Cambridge in popular culture">University of Cambridge in popular culture</a></div>
<p>The city has been the setting for all or part of several novels, including <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Adams" title="Douglas Adams">Douglas Adams</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Dirk_Gently%27s_Holistic_Detective_Agency" title="Dirk Gently&#39;s Holistic Detective Agency">Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Rose_Macaulay" title="Rose Macaulay">Rose Macaulay</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/They_Were_Defeated" title="They Were Defeated">They Were Defeated</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kate_Atkinson" title="Kate Atkinson">Kate Atkinson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Case_Histories" title="Case Histories">Case Histories</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Stott" title="Rebecca Stott">Rebecca Stott</a>'s <i>Ghostwalk</i><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Harris_(novelist)" title="Robert Harris (novelist)">Robert Harris</a>'s <i>Enigma</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Susanna_Gregory" title="Susanna Gregory">Susanna Gregory</a> wrote a series of novels set in 14th century Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Raverat" title="Gwen Raverat">Gwen Raverat</a>, the granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, talked about her late Victorian Cambridge childhood in her memoir <i><a href="/wiki/Period_Piece_(book)" title="Period Piece (book)">Period Piece</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_Climbers_of_Cambridge" title="The Night Climbers of Cambridge">The Night Climbers of Cambridge</a></i> is a book written by <a href="/wiki/Noel_Symington" class="mw-redirect" title="Noel Symington">Noel Symington</a> under the pseudonym "Whipplesnaith" about nocturnal climbing on the colleges and town buildings of Cambridge in the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fictionalised versions of Cambridge appear in <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Pearce" title="Philippa Pearce">Philippa Pearce</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tom%27s_Midnight_Garden" title="Tom&#39;s Midnight Garden">Tom's Midnight Garden</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Minnow_on_the_Say" title="Minnow on the Say">Minnow on the Say</a></i>, the city renamed as Castleford, and as the home of <a href="/wiki/Tom_Sharpe" title="Tom Sharpe">Tom Sharpe</a>'s fictional college in <i><a href="/wiki/Porterhouse_Blue" title="Porterhouse Blue">Porterhouse Blue</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> TV series <a href="/wiki/Grantchester_(TV_series)" title="Grantchester (TV series)"><i>Granchester</i></a> was partly filmed in Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG/220px-Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG/330px-Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG/440px-Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Addenbrooke%27s_hospital.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's Hospital</a></div></div></div>
<p>Cambridge is served by <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Cambridge University Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">Cambridge University Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a>, with several smaller medical centres in the city and a <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospital</a> at <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's</a>. Located on the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Biomedical_Campus" title="Cambridge Biomedical Campus">Cambridge Biomedical Campus</a>, Addenbrooke's is one of the largest hospitals in the United Kingdom and is a designated regional <a href="/wiki/Trauma_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Trauma centre">trauma centre</a>.
</p><p>The East of England Ambulance Service covers the city and has an ambulance station on Hills Road.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The smaller Brookfields Hospital stands on Mill Road.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_Constabulary" title="Cambridgeshire Constabulary">Cambridgeshire Constabulary</a> provides the city's policing; the main police station is at <a href="/wiki/Parkside,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Parkside, Cambridge">Parkside</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> adjacent to the city's <a href="/wiki/Fire_station" title="Fire station">fire station</a>, operated by <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Cambridgeshire Fire and Rescue Service">Cambridgeshire Fire and Rescue Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Water_Company" title="Cambridge Water Company">Cambridge Water Company</a> supplies water services to the city,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Anglian_Water" title="Anglian Water">Anglian Water</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Sewerage" title="Sewerage">sewerage</a> services.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> For the supply of electricity, Cambridge is part of the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England" title="East of England">East of England</a> region, for which the <a href="/wiki/Distribution_network_operator" title="Distribution network operator">distribution network operator</a> is <a href="/wiki/UK_Power_Networks" title="UK Power Networks">UK Power Networks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The city has no power stations, though a five-metre wind turbine, part of a <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Regional_College" title="Cambridge Regional College">Cambridge Regional College</a> development, can be seen in <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Hedges" title="King&#39;s Hedges">King's Hedges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Public_Libraries_Act_1850" title="Public Libraries Act 1850">Public Libraries Act 1850</a> the city's first public library, located on Jesus Lane, was opened in 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-Roach116-122_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach116-122-203">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> It was moved to the Guildhall in 1862,<sup id="cite_ref-Roach116-122_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roach116-122-203">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and is now located in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Arcade_(Cambridge)" title="Grand Arcade (Cambridge)">Grand Arcade</a> shopping centre. The library was reopened in September 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-libopen_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libopen-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> after having been closed for refurbishment for 33 months, more than twice as long as was forecast when the library closed for redevelopment in January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-libopen_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libopen-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018 the city contains six public libraries, run by the County Council.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_City_Cemetery" title="Cambridge City Cemetery">Cambridge City Cemetery</a> is located to the north of <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Road,_Cambridge" title="Newmarket Road, Cambridge">Newmarket Road</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CambridgeTownCentre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/CambridgeTownCentre.jpg/220px-CambridgeTownCentre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/CambridgeTownCentre.jpg/330px-CambridgeTownCentre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/CambridgeTownCentre.jpg/440px-CambridgeTownCentre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1081" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CambridgeTownCentre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Mary_the_Great_with_St_Michael,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary the Great with St Michael, Cambridge">Great St Mary's Church</a> marks the centre of Cambridge, while the <a href="/wiki/Senate_House_(University_of_Cambridge)" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate House (University of Cambridge)">Senate House</a> on the left is the centre of the University. <a href="/wiki/Gonville_and_Caius_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Gonville and Caius College">Gonville and Caius College</a> is in the background.</div></div></div>
<p>Cambridge has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_churches_in_Cambridge" title="List of churches in Cambridge">number of churches</a>, some of which form a significant part of the city's architectural landscape. Like the rest of Cambridgeshire it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Ely" title="Diocese of Ely">Diocese of Ely</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> A Cambridge-based family and youth organisation, <a href="/wiki/Romsey_Mill" title="Romsey Mill">Romsey Mill</a>, had its centre re-dedicated in 2007 by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_York" title="Archbishop of York">Archbishop of York</a>, and is quoted as an example of best practice in a study<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> into <a href="/wiki/Social_inclusion" class="mw-redirect" title="Social inclusion">social inclusion</a> by the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England_Regional_Assembly" title="East of England Regional Assembly">East of England Regional Assembly</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/St_Mary_the_Great_with_St_Michael,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="St Mary the Great with St Michael, Cambridge">Great St Mary's Church</a> has the status of "University Church".<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Many of the University colleges contain chapels that hold services according to the rites and ceremonies of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, while the chapel of <a href="/wiki/St_Edmund%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="St Edmund&#39;s College, Cambridge">St Edmund's College</a> is Roman Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The city also has a number of <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Theological_Federation" title="Cambridge Theological Federation">theological colleges</a> training clergy for <a href="/wiki/Ordination" title="Ordination">ordination</a> into a number of denominations, with affiliations to both the University of Cambridge and <a href="/wiki/Anglia_Ruskin_University" title="Anglia Ruskin University">Anglia Ruskin University</a>.
</p><p>Cambridge is in the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_East_Anglia" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of East Anglia">Diocese of East Anglia</a> and is served by the large <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a> <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_and_the_English_Martyrs_Church" title="Our Lady and the English Martyrs Church">Our Lady and the English Martyrs Church</a> at the junction of Hills Road and Lensfield Road, <a href="/wiki/St_Laurence%27s_Church,_Cambridge" title="St Laurence&#39;s Church, Cambridge">St Laurence's</a> on Milton Road, St Vincent De Paul Church on Ditton Lane and by the church of St Philip Howard, in Cherry Hinton Road.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> There is a <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Patriarchate" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Patriarchate">Russian Orthodox</a> church under the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Diocese_of_Sourozh" title="Russian Orthodox Diocese of Sourozh">Diocese of Sourozh</a> who worship at the chapel of <a href="/wiki/Westcott_House,_Cambridge" title="Westcott House, Cambridge">Westcott House</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox Church</a> holds services at the church St Athanasios under the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Thyateira_and_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Thyateira and Great Britain">Archdiocese of Thyateira and Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> There are three <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quaker</a> Meetings in Cambridge, located on Jesus Lane, Hartington Grove, and a Meeting called "Oast House" that meets in Pembroke College.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox</a> synagogue and Jewish student centre is located on Thompson's Lane, operated jointly by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge_Traditional_Jewish_Congregation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cambridge Traditional Jewish Congregation (page does not exist)">Cambridge Traditional Jewish Congregation</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge_University_Jewish_Society&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cambridge University Jewish Society (page does not exist)">Cambridge University Jewish Society</a>, which is affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Jewish_Students" title="Union of Jewish Students">Union of Jewish Students</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The Beth Shalom <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">Reform</a> synagogue which previously met at a local school,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> has recently opened a purpose-built synagogue.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> There is also a student-led egalitarian <a href="/wiki/Minyan" title="Minyan">minyan</a> which holds services on Friday evenings.
</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abu_Bakr_Jamia_Islamic_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abu Bakr Jamia Islamic Centre (page does not exist)">Abu Bakr Jamia Islamic Centre</a> on Mawson Road and the Omar Faruque Mosque and Cultural Centre in Kings Hedges<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> serve the city's community of around 4,000 Muslims until a planned new mosque is built.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> centre was opened in the former <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Barnwell,_Cambridge" title="Theatre Royal, Barnwell, Cambridge">Barnwell Theatre</a> on Newmarket Road in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> shrine was opened in 2010 at the Bharat Bhavan Indian cultural centre off <a href="/wiki/Mill_Road,_Cambridge" title="Mill Road, Cambridge">Mill Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twinned_cities">Twinned cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Twinned cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cambridge is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with two cities. Like Cambridge, both have universities and are also similar in population; <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg" title="Heidelberg">Heidelberg</a>, Germany since 1965,<sup id="cite_ref-twintown_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twintown-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Szeged" title="Szeged">Szeged</a>, Hungary since 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-twintown_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twintown-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Panoramic_gallery">Panoramic gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Panoramic gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Weather station is located 3 miles (5&#160;km) from the Cambridge city centre.</span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
